In this chapter, we have explored the importance of public roundtables in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development and the just city. We have discussed the benefits of bringing together diverse stakeholders to discuss and address issues related to economic development, and how this can lead to more informed and effective decision-making. We have also highlighted the role of local policies in shaping the outcomes of these roundtables, and how they can be used to create a more equitable and inclusive environment for all members of the community.

Through the use of public roundtables, we have seen how local governments can foster a sense of community ownership and participation in economic development initiatives. By involving a diverse group of stakeholders, including community members, businesses, and non-profit organizations, these roundtables can provide a platform for open and honest dialogue, leading to more comprehensive and sustainable solutions. Additionally, by incorporating equity and inclusion principles into the policies and guidelines used in these roundtables, we can ensure that the needs and perspectives of marginalized and underrepresented groups are taken into account.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to recognize that public roundtables are just one tool in the larger process of creating a more equitable and inclusive city. It is crucial for local governments to continue to prioritize and invest in initiatives that promote equity and inclusion, and to use public roundtables as a means of engaging and empowering the community in this process. By working together and utilizing local policies, we can create a more just and prosperous city for all.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City

### Introduction:

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of a just city has become increasingly important. As urban populations continue to grow and resources become scarcer, it is crucial for cities to address issues of equity and inclusion in order to create a sustainable and livable future for all residents. This chapter will explore the role of local policy in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development, and how it can contribute to creating a just city.

The concept of a just city is rooted in the idea of fairness and equality for all members of the community. It recognizes that every individual has unique needs and circumstances, and that these should be taken into account when creating policies and programs. This chapter will delve into the various factors that contribute to equity and inclusion, such as race, income, and access to resources, and how local policies can address these issues.

One of the key ways in which local policy can promote equity and inclusion is through economic development. By creating policies that support job creation, affordable housing, and access to education and healthcare, cities can help to alleviate poverty and create opportunities for marginalized communities. This chapter will explore the different strategies and initiatives that can be implemented at the local level to promote economic development and address issues of equity and inclusion.

Furthermore, this chapter will also discuss the importance of community engagement and participation in the policy-making process. By involving diverse groups of stakeholders, including community members, businesses, and non-profit organizations, cities can ensure that their policies are inclusive and responsive to the needs of all residents. This chapter will provide examples of successful community engagement initiatives and how they have contributed to creating a more equitable and inclusive city.

In conclusion, this chapter will provide a comprehensive overview of the role of local policy in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development and creating a just city. By understanding the various factors that contribute to these issues and implementing effective policies and initiatives, cities can create a more equitable and inclusive future for all residents.

The written evaluation can provide more detailed feedback and suggestions for improvement.

We must be open to feedback and use it to improve our presentations and strategies. It is important to remember that feedback is meant to help us, not criticize us. We should take notes on the feedback we receive and use it to make revisions to our presentations.

We should also consider the feedback when preparing for our final presentations, as it can help us improve our strategies and effectively communicate our key takeaways.

We will also examine the role of local governments in promoting equity and inclusion, and the challenges they face in implementing policies and programs. Additionally, we will discuss the importance of community engagement and collaboration in creating a more equitable and inclusive city.

As we navigate through the complex and ever-evolving landscape of equity and inclusion, it is important to keep in mind that there is no one-size-fits-all solution. Each community is unique and requires a tailored approach to address its specific needs and challenges. By understanding the principles and strategies outlined in this chapter, local governments can create a more equitable and inclusive city for all their residents.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 14: Equity and Inclusion:




### Introduction

Urban planning and public health are two critical components of creating a just city. The way a city is designed and managed can have a significant impact on the health and well-being of its residents. This chapter will explore the intersection of urban planning and public health, and how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development.

The chapter will begin by discussing the role of urban planning in shaping the health of a city. It will delve into the various factors that urban planners must consider when designing a city, such as access to healthcare, transportation, and housing. The chapter will also examine how urban planning can be used to address health disparities and promote health equity.

Next, the chapter will explore the relationship between public health and economic development. It will discuss how economic development can impact the health of a community, and how public health can be used as a tool for economic development. The chapter will also examine the role of local policies in promoting economic development and improving public health.

Finally, the chapter will discuss the importance of equity and inclusion in economic development and public health. It will explore how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion, and how these efforts can contribute to creating a just city. The chapter will also examine case studies of cities that have successfully implemented equity and inclusion strategies in their urban planning and public health policies.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the role of urban planning and public health in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development and creating a just city. It will serve as a guide for policymakers, urban planners, and public health professionals in developing and implementing effective policies and strategies for creating a healthier and more equitable city.




### Section: 14.1 Urban Planning and Public Health:

Urban planning plays a crucial role in promoting public health and creating a just city. It involves the design and management of the physical environment, including land use, transportation, and infrastructure, to improve the quality of life for all residents. In this section, we will explore the intersection of urban planning and public health, and how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development.

#### 14.1a The Intersection of Urban Planning and Public Health

Urban planning and public health are closely intertwined. The physical environment of a city can have a significant impact on the health and well-being of its residents. For example, access to green spaces and parks has been linked to improved mental and physical health, while exposure to air pollution and extreme heat events can have negative effects on health.

One of the key considerations in urban planning is the impact on public health. Urban climatology, the study of climate and its effects on urban areas, plays a crucial role in decision-making for municipal planning and policy. It helps planners understand the potential impacts of pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater modeling on public health.

Another important aspect of urban planning and public health is the use of geographic information systems (GIS). GIS is a powerful tool that allows planners to analyze and visualize data, such as health outcomes and environmental factors, to inform decision-making. By using GIS, planners can identify areas with high levels of pollution or lack of access to green spaces and develop targeted interventions to improve public health.

#### 14.1b The Role of Local Policies in Promoting Equity and Inclusion in Economic Development

Local policies play a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development. They provide a framework for decision-making and guide the actions of urban planners and policymakers. By incorporating equity and inclusion principles into local policies, cities can create a more just and equitable environment for all residents.

One example of a local policy that promotes equity and inclusion is the inclusionary zoning policy. This policy requires developers to include a certain percentage of affordable housing units in new developments, ensuring that low-income residents have access to affordable housing. This can help address the issue of housing affordability and reduce health disparities related to housing.

Another important policy is the complete streets policy, which aims to create safe and accessible streets for all modes of transportation, including walking, biking, and public transit. This can improve public health by promoting physical activity and reducing air pollution from vehicle emissions. Additionally, complete streets can also address issues of equity and inclusion by providing equal access to transportation for all residents, regardless of their income or mode of transportation.

#### 14.1c Case Studies of Urban Planning and Public Health

To further illustrate the impact of urban planning on public health, let's examine some case studies. In the city of Portland, Oregon, the implementation of a complete streets policy has led to improved public health outcomes. By prioritizing pedestrian and bicycle infrastructure, the city has seen a decrease in vehicle miles traveled and a corresponding decrease in air pollution. This has also led to increased physical activity among residents, resulting in improved mental and physical health.

In another example, the city of Boston, Massachusetts, has implemented an inclusionary zoning policy to address the issue of housing affordability. This policy has resulted in the creation of over 1,000 affordable housing units, providing low-income residents with access to safe and affordable housing. This has also helped reduce health disparities related to housing, as low-income residents are now able to access better quality housing.

#### 14.1d Conclusion

In conclusion, urban planning and public health are closely intertwined, and local policies play a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development. By incorporating equity and inclusion principles into local policies, cities can create a more just and equitable environment for all residents, leading to improved public health outcomes. Case studies from cities like Portland and Boston demonstrate the positive impact of urban planning on public health and the importance of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion. 





### Section: 14.1 Urban Planning and Public Health:

Urban planning plays a crucial role in promoting public health and creating a just city. It involves the design and management of the physical environment, including land use, transportation, and infrastructure, to improve the quality of life for all residents. In this section, we will explore the intersection of urban planning and public health, and how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development.

#### 14.1a The Intersection of Urban Planning and Public Health

Urban planning and public health are closely intertwined. The physical environment of a city can have a significant impact on the health and well-being of its residents. For example, access to green spaces and parks has been linked to improved mental and physical health, while exposure to air pollution and extreme heat events can have negative effects on health.

One of the key considerations in urban planning is the impact on public health. Urban climatology, the study of climate and its effects on urban areas, plays a crucial role in decision-making for municipal planning and policy. It helps planners understand the potential impacts of pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater modeling on public health.

Another important aspect of urban planning and public health is the use of geographic information systems (GIS). GIS is a powerful tool that allows planners to analyze and visualize data, such as health outcomes and environmental factors, to inform decision-making. By using GIS, planners can identify areas with high levels of pollution or lack of access to green spaces and develop targeted interventions to improve public health.

#### 14.1b Health Impact Assessments in Urban Planning

Health impact assessments (HIAs) are a crucial tool in urban planning that helps evaluate the potential health impacts of proposed developments or policies. HIAs are used to identify potential health risks and benefits, and to develop strategies to mitigate any negative impacts. They are often required by local governments as part of the planning process to ensure that public health is considered in all development decisions.

HIAs are typically conducted by a team of experts, including urban planners, public health professionals, and other stakeholders. They involve a thorough analysis of the proposed development or policy, including its potential impacts on air quality, noise levels, access to green spaces, and other factors that may affect public health. The results of the HIA are then used to inform decision-making and develop strategies to address any potential health impacts.

#### 14.1c Case Studies of Urban Planning and Public Health

To further illustrate the importance of urban planning in promoting public health, let's examine two case studies: the development of a new park in a low-income neighborhood and the redesign of a busy street to improve pedestrian safety.

In the first case study, a new park is being developed in a low-income neighborhood with limited access to green spaces. The HIA for this project identified potential benefits such as increased physical activity and improved air quality, as well as potential risks such as increased noise levels and potential for crime in the park. To address these concerns, the HIA team developed a plan for a multi-use park with a variety of activities to encourage physical activity, as well as measures to mitigate noise and crime.

In the second case study, a busy street is being redesigned to improve pedestrian safety. The HIA for this project identified potential benefits such as reduced traffic injuries and improved air quality, as well as potential risks such as increased traffic congestion and potential for noise pollution. To address these concerns, the HIA team developed a plan for a complete street design, which includes dedicated bike lanes, wider sidewalks, and traffic calming measures.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering public health in urban planning decisions. By conducting HIAs and involving a diverse group of stakeholders, urban planners can ensure that developments and policies are designed to promote the health and well-being of all residents. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of urban planning and public health, and how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development and create a just city. We have discussed the importance of considering the health impacts of urban planning decisions, and how urban planning can be used as a tool to address health disparities and promote health equity. We have also examined the role of public participation and community engagement in the urban planning process, and how it can lead to more inclusive and equitable outcomes.

One key takeaway from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to urban planning that takes into account the complex interplay between economic development, public health, and social equity. This requires collaboration and communication between various stakeholders, including government agencies, community organizations, and residents. By working together, we can create more livable and healthy cities for all members of our communities.

#### Exercise 1: Analyzing the Health Impacts of Urban Planning Decisions
Choose a recent urban planning decision in your city or a nearby city. Research the potential health impacts of this decision and discuss how it aligns with or conflicts with principles of equity and inclusion.

#### Exercise 2: Community Engagement in Urban Planning
Interview a community organization or resident group that has been involved in the urban planning process in your city. Ask about their experiences with public participation and how it has impacted the outcome of the planning process.

#### Exercise 3: The Role of Urban Planning in Addressing Health Disparities

#### Exercise 4: Creating a Just City through Urban Planning

## Chapter: Chapter 15: Urban Planning and Transportation

### Introduction

Urban planning and transportation are two crucial components of creating a just and equitable city. It is a key factor in determining access to jobs, education, healthcare, and other opportunities. However, transportation planning is often overlooked or under-resourced, leading to inefficient and inequitable systems. This chapter will delve into the complexities of transportation planning and how it can be used as a tool for promoting equity and inclusion in the city.

We will also examine the relationship between urban planning and transportation. Urban planning sets the framework for how a city is designed and developed, and transportation planning is a crucial aspect of this process. By considering transportation in the early stages of urban planning, we can create more sustainable and equitable cities. ## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become increasingly important in shaping the policies and strategies of local governments. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial for policymakers to address the issues of equity and inclusion in order to create a just and sustainable city for all its residents. This chapter will explore the intersection of equity and inclusion in the context of local policy-driven strategies for economic development.

Equity and inclusion are two fundamental principles that guide the development of any just city. Equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of the community, while inclusion aims to ensure that all individuals have a voice and are able to participate fully in the decision-making process. These principles are essential for creating a city that is equitable and inclusive, where all residents have equal access to opportunities and resources.

The chapter will delve into the various ways in which local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development. This includes policies related to housing, education, employment, and healthcare. By examining these policies, we can gain a better understanding of how they can be used to address the root causes of inequality and exclusion in the city.

Furthermore, the chapter will also explore the role of community engagement and participation in shaping local policies. As the concept of equity and inclusion is deeply rooted in the principles of democracy, it is crucial for policymakers to involve the community in the decision-making process. This not only ensures that the policies are reflective of the needs and concerns of the community, but also promotes a sense of ownership and accountability among residents.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of the role of equity and inclusion in local policy-driven strategies for economic development. By understanding the principles and policies that guide the creation of a just city, we can work towards creating a more equitable and inclusive society for all.


## Chapter 1:5: Equity and Inclusion in Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development:




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of urban planning and public health, and how local policies can be used to address issues of equity and inclusion in economic development and the creation of just cities. We have discussed the importance of considering the health impacts of urban planning decisions, and how these decisions can either exacerbate or alleviate health disparities. We have also examined the role of community engagement and participation in the planning process, and how it can lead to more equitable and inclusive outcomes.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to urban planning that takes into account the social, economic, and environmental factors that influence public health. This requires collaboration between different stakeholders, including government agencies, community organizations, and health providers. By working together, we can create more just and healthy cities that promote equity and inclusion for all residents.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become increasingly important in shaping the policies and strategies of local governments. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial for policymakers to address the issues of equity and inclusion in order to create a just and sustainable city for all its residents. This chapter will explore the intersection of equity and inclusion in the context of local policy-driven strategies for economic development.

Equity and inclusion are two fundamental principles that guide the development of any just city. Equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of the community, while inclusion aims to ensure that all individuals have a voice and are able to participate fully in the decision-making process. These principles are essential for creating a city that is equitable and inclusive, where all residents have equal access to opportunities and resources.

The chapter will delve into the various ways in which local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development. This includes policies related to housing, education, employment, and healthcare. By examining these policies, we can gain a better understanding of how they can be used to address the root causes of inequality and exclusion in the city.

Furthermore, the chapter will also explore the role of community engagement and participation in shaping local policies. As the concept of equity and inclusion is deeply rooted in the principles of democracy, it is crucial for policymakers to involve the community in the decision-making process. This not only ensures that the policies are reflective of the needs and concerns of the community, but also promotes a sense of ownership and accountability among residents.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of the role of equity and inclusion in local policy-driven strategies for economic development. By understanding the principles and policies that guide the creation of a just city, we can work towards creating a more equitable and inclusive society for all.


## Chapter 1:5: Equity and Inclusion in Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development:




### Introduction

Housing policy plays a crucial role in shaping the economic development and social fabric of a city. It is a complex and multifaceted issue that intersects with various other policy areas such as land use, transportation, and social services. In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between housing policy and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote economic development and create a just city.

The concept of equity in housing refers to the fair distribution of housing opportunities and resources among different groups of people. It is a fundamental principle that guides housing policy and is essential for creating a just city. However, achieving equity in housing is a challenging task, as it requires addressing a range of complex and interconnected issues.

One of the key factors that contribute to housing equity is the availability of affordable housing. Affordable housing refers to housing that is within the financial means of low and moderate-income households. It is a critical component of a just city, as it ensures that all members of the community have access to safe and decent housing.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various aspects of housing policy and equity, including the role of local governments, the impact of housing policies on different groups, and the challenges and opportunities in promoting housing equity. We will also explore the relationship between housing policy and other policy areas, such as economic development and social services.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of housing policy and equity, and how it can be used as a tool for promoting economic development and creating a just city. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complexities of housing policy and equity, and the role it plays in shaping our cities.




### Subsection: 15.1a Understanding Housing Policy

Housing policy is a crucial aspect of urban planning and development. It is a set of rules, regulations, and guidelines that govern the provision of housing in a city. These policies are designed to address issues of affordability, accessibility, and quality of housing. They also aim to promote equity and inclusivity in the housing market.

#### The Role of Housing Policy in Economic Development

Housing policy plays a significant role in economic development. It affects the availability and affordability of housing, which in turn impacts the cost of living and the standard of living for residents. Housing policy also influences the overall economic health of a city by affecting the demand for housing and the construction industry.

For instance, policies that promote affordable housing can help to reduce the cost of living for residents, making it more affordable for them to live in the city. This can attract more people to the city, increasing the demand for housing and stimulating the construction industry. On the other hand, policies that restrict the supply of housing can lead to housing shortages and rising housing prices, making it more difficult for people to afford housing and potentially hindering economic development.

#### The Impact of Housing Policy on Equity and Inclusion

Housing policy also has a significant impact on equity and inclusion. Equity in housing refers to the fair distribution of housing opportunities and resources among different groups of people. Inclusion in housing refers to the ability of all members of the community to participate in the housing market and have access to safe and decent housing.

Housing policies can promote equity and inclusion by addressing issues of affordability and accessibility. For example, policies that provide subsidies or tax incentives for affordable housing can help to make housing more accessible to low-income households. Similarly, policies that require developers to include a certain percentage of affordable units in new developments can help to address issues of affordability and promote equity.

#### The Challenges and Opportunities in Housing Policy

Despite its importance, implementing effective housing policies can be challenging. One of the main challenges is balancing the competing interests of different stakeholders, such as developers, residents, and the government. This requires careful consideration of the potential impacts of policies on different groups and finding ways to address their concerns.

However, there are also opportunities in housing policy. For instance, the use of technology and data can help to improve the efficiency and effectiveness of housing policies. Data-driven approaches can help to identify areas of high housing demand and inform decisions about where to focus resources. Technology can also be used to streamline processes and reduce costs, making housing policies more sustainable and affordable.

In conclusion, housing policy plays a crucial role in economic development and promoting equity and inclusion in the housing market. It is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires careful consideration and collaboration among different stakeholders. By understanding the principles and strategies of housing policy, local governments can create more equitable and inclusive housing markets and contribute to the overall well-being of their communities.





### Subsection: 15.1b Housing Affordability and Equity

Housing affordability is a critical aspect of housing policy and equity. It refers to the ability of households to access and maintain decent, safe, and affordable housing without experiencing housing stress. Housing stress occurs when a household is forced to spend more than 30% of its income on housing costs, including rent or mortgage payments, utilities, and maintenance. This can lead to financial hardship and difficulty meeting other basic needs, such as food, healthcare, and education.

#### The Relationship between Housing Affordability and Equity

Housing affordability is closely linked to equity. Equity in housing refers to the fair distribution of housing opportunities and resources among different groups of people. Housing affordability is a key factor in achieving housing equity. If certain groups of people, such as low-income households or minority groups, face barriers to accessing affordable housing, this can exacerbate existing inequalities and limit their opportunities for social and economic participation.

#### Housing Affordability and Equity in the United States

In the United States, housing affordability and equity have been major challenges. The National Association of Realtors (NAR) publishes a monthly Housing Affordability Index, which measures whether or not a typical family earns enough income to qualify for a mortgage loan on a typical home at the national and regional levels. The index is calculated based on the most recent price and income data.

According to the NAR, a value of 100 on the Housing Affordability Index means that a family with the median income has exactly enough income to qualify for a mortgage on a median-priced home. An index above 100 signifies that family earning the median income has more than enough income to qualify for a mortgage loan on a median-priced home, assuming a 20% down payment and a qualifying ratio of 25%.

However, despite these efforts, housing affordability remains a significant issue in the United States. The Center for Neighborhood Technology's Housing + Transportation Affordability Index, which provides a "comprehensive view of affordability that includes both the cost of housing and the cost of transportation at the neighborhood level," has found that many neighborhoods in the United States are unaffordable for low-income households. This highlights the need for more comprehensive and inclusive housing policies that address both housing affordability and equity.

The Center for Neighborhood Technology's Housing + Transportation Affordability Index, which provides a "comprehensive view of affordability that includes both the cost of housing and the cost of transportation at the neighborhood level," has found that many neighborhoods in the United States are unaffordable for low-income households. This highlights the need for more comprehensive and inclusive housing policies that address both housing affordability and equity.

#### Housing Affordability and Equity in the United States

In the United States, housing affordability and equity have been major challenges. The National Association of Realtors (NAR) publishes a monthly Housing Affordability Index, which measures whether or not a typical family earns enough income to qualify for a mortgage loan on a typical home at the national and regional levels. The index is calculated based on the most recent price and income data.

According to the NAR, a value of 100 on the Housing Affordability Index means that a family with the median income has exactly enough income to qualify for a mortgage on a median-priced home. An index above 100 signifies that family earning the median income has more than enough income to qualify for a mortgage loan on a median-priced home, assuming a 20% down payment and a qualifying ratio of 25%.

### Subsection: 15.1c Strategies for Equitable Housing Policy

In order to address the challenges of housing affordability and equity, local governments can implement a variety of strategies. These strategies can be broadly categorized into three areas: increasing housing supply, providing affordable housing options, and promoting fair housing practices.

#### Increasing Housing Supply

One of the most effective ways to increase housing affordability is by increasing the supply of housing. This can be achieved through various means, such as relaxing zoning laws, allowing for denser development, and providing incentives for developers to build affordable housing units. By increasing the supply of housing, the demand for housing can be spread out, leading to a decrease in housing prices.

#### Providing Affordable Housing Options

In addition to increasing housing supply, local governments can also provide affordable housing options directly. This can be done through public housing programs, housing vouchers, or tax credits for affordable housing development. These programs can help low-income households access decent, safe, and affordable housing.

#### Promoting Fair Housing Practices

Local governments can also play a role in promoting fair housing practices. This can be achieved through anti-discrimination laws, affordable housing policies, and community land trusts. Anti-discrimination laws can help prevent discrimination in the housing market, while affordable housing policies can ensure that affordable housing options are available in all neighborhoods. Community land trusts, on the other hand, can help preserve affordable housing options by removing housing units from the speculative market.

#### Case Studies of Equitable Housing Policy

To further illustrate these strategies, let's look at some case studies of local governments that have successfully implemented equitable housing policies.

##### Case Study 1: Portland, Oregon

In Portland, Oregon, the city government has implemented a variety of strategies to address housing affordability and equity. This includes relaxing zoning laws to allow for denser development, providing incentives for developers to build affordable housing units, and implementing a community land trust to preserve affordable housing options. As a result, Portland has seen a significant increase in housing supply and a decrease in housing prices, making housing more affordable for low-income households.

##### Case Study 2: San Francisco, California

In San Francisco, the city government has implemented a housing voucher program to provide affordable housing options for low-income households. This program has helped thousands of households access decent, safe, and affordable housing. In addition, the city has also implemented anti-discrimination laws and affordable housing policies to promote fair housing practices.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, local governments play a crucial role in addressing housing affordability and equity. By implementing strategies such as increasing housing supply, providing affordable housing options, and promoting fair housing practices, local governments can help create more equitable housing policies and contribute to a more just city. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex and multifaceted issue of housing policy and equity. We have discussed the historical context of housing policies in the United States, the current challenges faced by marginalized communities in accessing safe and affordable housing, and the potential solutions that can be implemented at the local level to address these issues.

We have seen how housing policies have evolved over time, from the discriminatory practices of the past to the more inclusive policies of today. However, despite these advancements, there are still significant barriers to equitable housing for marginalized communities. These barriers include systemic discrimination, gentrification, and the lack of affordable housing options in many urban areas.

To address these challenges, we have discussed various strategies that local governments can implement, such as affordable housing programs, rent control policies, and anti-discrimination laws. We have also highlighted the importance of community involvement and collaboration in creating and implementing effective housing policies.

As we move forward, it is crucial for local governments to continue addressing housing policy and equity as a top priority. By implementing evidence-based policies and involving marginalized communities in the decision-making process, we can create more equitable and inclusive housing options for all.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 16: Equity and Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

Transportation planning plays a crucial role in shaping the economic development and social fabric of a city. It is a complex process that involves the coordination of various stakeholders, including government agencies, private sector entities, and community groups. The goal of transportation planning is to create a comprehensive and sustainable transportation system that meets the needs of all members of the community, regardless of their socio-economic status.

In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of transportation planning and equity. We will delve into the various factors that contribute to transportation equity, including accessibility, affordability, and inclusivity. We will also examine the role of local policies in promoting transportation equity and how these policies can be used to address transportation disparities.

The chapter will begin by providing an overview of transportation planning and its importance in economic development and the just city. We will then delve into the concept of transportation equity and its relationship with transportation planning. We will also discuss the challenges and opportunities in promoting transportation equity, and how local policies can be used to address these issues.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of transportation planning and equity, and how local policies can be used to create a more equitable and inclusive transportation system. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complexities of transportation planning and how it can be used to promote equity and inclusion in their communities.




### Section: 16.1 Transportation Planning and Equity:

Transportation planning is a crucial aspect of urban development that has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of different communities within a city. It involves the coordination of various stakeholders, including government agencies, private sector entities, and community groups, to create a comprehensive and sustainable transportation system that meets the needs of all members of the community.

#### 16.1a The Role of Transportation in Urban Equity

Transportation plays a critical role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. It provides access to essential services such as education, healthcare, and employment opportunities, and is a key factor in determining the quality of life for individuals and communities. However, transportation planning has often been criticized for perpetuating and exacerbating existing social and economic inequalities.

One of the main ways in which transportation planning can impact equity is through its influence on housing affordability. As mentioned in the related context, there is a concern that anti-sprawl policies, such as urban intensification and smart growth, may lead to increased housing prices. This can have a disproportionate impact on low-income and minority communities, who may already face challenges in finding affordable housing options.

In addition to housing affordability, transportation planning also plays a role in promoting or hindering social equity. The distribution of transportation options and services can have a significant impact on the ability of different communities to access essential services and opportunities. For example, in urban centers like Los Angeles and San Francisco, minority areas often have limited transportation options, leading to overcrowded and unsafe transportation routes. This not only affects the daily lives of these communities but also limits their ability to move out of urban areas and access better opportunities.

Transportation planning also has a direct impact on economic equity. The distribution of transportation options and services can affect the ability of different communities to access employment opportunities. This can have a significant impact on the economic well-being of individuals and communities, particularly those from low-income and minority backgrounds.

#### 16.1b The Paradox of Intensification and its Impact on Equity

The concept of the paradox of intensification, as proposed by Melia et al. (2011), highlights the complex relationship between transportation planning and equity. While planning policies that increase population densities in urban areas can reduce car use, the effect is weak, and doubling the population density of a particular area will not halve the frequency or distance of car use. This means that while intensification can help reduce car use, it may not be enough to address the transportation disparities faced by low-income and minority communities.

#### 16.1c Case Studies of Transportation Planning and Equity

To further understand the impact of transportation planning on equity, let us examine some case studies. In Portland, Oregon, the implementation of anti-sprawl policies has led to a decrease in housing affordability, particularly for low-income and minority communities. This has raised concerns about the potential negative impact of these policies on social and economic equity.

On the other hand, in Curitiba, Brazil, the implementation of a comprehensive transportation plan has led to significant improvements in equity. The city has implemented a bus rapid transit system, known as the "Tube," which provides affordable and efficient transportation options for all members of the community. This has not only improved access to essential services and opportunities but has also led to a decrease in car use and traffic congestion, promoting a more sustainable and equitable transportation system.

#### 16.1d Conclusion

Transportation planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. It has the potential to address transportation disparities faced by low-income and minority communities, but it can also perpetuate and exacerbate existing social and economic inequalities. Therefore, it is essential for transportation planners to consider the potential impact of their policies on equity and work towards creating a more equitable and inclusive transportation system for all members of the community.





### Section: 16.1 Transportation Planning and Equity:

Transportation planning is a crucial aspect of urban development that has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of different communities within a city. It involves the coordination of various stakeholders, including government agencies, private sector entities, and community groups, to create a comprehensive and sustainable transportation system that meets the needs of all members of the community.

#### 16.1a The Role of Transportation in Urban Equity

Transportation plays a critical role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. It provides access to essential services such as education, healthcare, and employment opportunities, and is a key factor in determining the quality of life for individuals and communities. However, transportation planning has often been criticized for perpetuating and exacerbating existing social and economic inequalities.

One of the main ways in which transportation planning can impact equity is through its influence on housing affordability. As mentioned in the related context, there is a concern that anti-sprawl policies, such as urban intensification and smart growth, may lead to increased housing prices. This can have a disproportionate impact on low-income and minority communities, who may already face challenges in finding affordable housing options.

In addition to housing affordability, transportation planning also plays a role in promoting or hindering social equity. The distribution of transportation options and services can have a significant impact on the ability of different communities to access essential services and opportunities. For example, in urban centers like Los Angeles and San Francisco, minority areas often have limited transportation options, leading to overcrowded and unsafe transportation routes. This not only affects the daily lives of these communities but also limits their ability to move out of urban areas and access better opportunities.

#### 16.1b Equitable Transportation Planning Strategies

To address the issue of transportation equity, it is important to implement equitable transportation planning strategies. These strategies aim to promote fair and equal access to transportation services for all members of the community, regardless of their socio-economic status or ethnicity. One such strategy is the use of transportation demand management (TDM) policies.

TDM policies aim to reduce the number of single-occupancy vehicles (SOVs) on the road and promote the use of alternative modes of transportation, such as public transit, walking, and biking. This can help alleviate traffic congestion and reduce air pollution, while also promoting social equity by providing more transportation options for low-income and minority communities.

Another equitable transportation planning strategy is the use of transit-oriented development (TOD). TOD involves the development of compact, walkable, and transit-friendly communities that are designed to reduce the need for personal vehicles. This can help promote social equity by providing more affordable housing options and improving access to essential services for low-income and minority communities.

In addition to these strategies, it is important for transportation planners to consider the potential impacts of their policies on different communities. This can be achieved through community engagement and participation, where community members are involved in the decision-making process and have a say in the design and implementation of transportation projects.

Overall, equitable transportation planning is crucial for promoting social equity and inclusion in urban areas. By implementing strategies such as TDM and TOD, and involving community members in the decision-making process, we can create a more just and sustainable transportation system for all.





### Section: 16.1 Transportation Planning and Equity:

Transportation planning is a crucial aspect of urban development that has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of different communities within a city. It involves the coordination of various stakeholders, including government agencies, private sector entities, and community groups, to create a comprehensive and sustainable transportation system that meets the needs of all members of the community.

#### 16.1a The Role of Transportation in Urban Equity

Transportation plays a critical role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. It provides access to essential services such as education, healthcare, and employment opportunities, and is a key factor in determining the quality of life for individuals and communities. However, transportation planning has often been criticized for perpetuating and exacerbating existing social and economic inequalities.

One of the main ways in which transportation planning can impact equity is through its influence on housing affordability. As mentioned in the related context, there is a concern that anti-sprawl policies, such as urban intensification and smart growth, may lead to increased housing prices. This can have a disproportionate impact on low-income and minority communities, who may already face challenges in finding affordable housing options.

In addition to housing affordability, transportation planning also plays a role in promoting or hindering social equity. The distribution of transportation options and services can have a significant impact on the ability of different communities to access essential services and opportunities. For example, in urban centers like Los Angeles and San Francisco, minority areas often have limited transportation options, leading to overcrowded and unsafe transportation routes. This not only affects the daily lives of these communities but also limits their ability to move out of urban areas and access better opportunities.

#### 16.1b The Role of Transportation in Economic Development

Transportation planning also plays a crucial role in economic development. It is essential for creating a well-connected and efficient transportation system that supports economic growth and job creation. A reliable and accessible transportation system can attract businesses and investors, leading to job opportunities and economic prosperity.

However, transportation planning can also have a significant impact on economic equity. The distribution of transportation options and services can affect the ability of different communities to access job opportunities and economic resources. For example, in cities with limited public transportation options, low-income and minority communities may face barriers to accessing job opportunities, leading to higher unemployment rates and economic disparities.

#### 16.1c Case Studies in Equitable Transportation Planning

To better understand the role of transportation planning in promoting equity and inclusion, let's examine some case studies from different cities around the world.

##### Case Study 1: Portland, Oregon

Portland, Oregon has been recognized as a leader in sustainable and equitable transportation planning. The city has implemented policies and programs that prioritize public transportation, walking, and biking, while also addressing issues of affordability and accessibility. The city's transit system, TriMet, offers a low-income fare program for eligible riders, and has also implemented a first-mile, last-mile program to provide transportation options for those who may not have access to a car. Additionally, Portland has implemented a complete streets policy, which aims to create safe and accessible streets for all modes of transportation, including pedestrians, cyclists, and public transit.

##### Case Study 2: Curitiba, Brazil

Curitiba, Brazil is known for its innovative and equitable transportation planning. The city has implemented a comprehensive bus rapid transit system, known as the "Tube," which provides fast and reliable transportation options for over 70% of the city's population. The Tube also offers a low-income fare program for eligible riders. In addition, Curitiba has implemented a network of bike lanes and pedestrian-friendly streets, making it one of the most walkable and bikeable cities in the world.

##### Case Study 3: Hanoi, Vietnam

Hanoi, Vietnam has faced challenges in its transportation planning due to rapid urbanization and limited resources. However, the city has made significant progress in promoting equity and inclusion through its transportation policies. The city has implemented a bus rapid transit system, known as the "Green Bus," which provides affordable and accessible transportation options for low-income and minority communities. In addition, Hanoi has implemented a complete streets policy, which aims to create safe and accessible streets for all modes of transportation.

#### 16.1d Conclusion

Transportation planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. It is essential for creating a well-connected and efficient transportation system that meets the needs of all members of the community. By prioritizing equity and inclusion in transportation planning, cities can create a more just and sustainable future for all.





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of transportation planning and equity, and how local policies can be used to address these issues. We have discussed the importance of considering equity in transportation planning, as transportation plays a crucial role in accessing employment, education, healthcare, and other opportunities. We have also examined the various factors that contribute to transportation equity, such as income, race, and disability.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a comprehensive and inclusive transportation planning process. This involves engaging all stakeholders, particularly those from marginalized communities, in the decision-making process. By doing so, we can ensure that the needs and concerns of all community members are taken into account, and that transportation policies are equitable and just.

Another important aspect of transportation planning for equity is the consideration of transportation equity metrics. These metrics can help us measure and track progress towards transportation equity, and inform decision-making. By using metrics such as the Transportation Equity Index and the Transportation Equity Score, we can assess the equity of transportation policies and make necessary adjustments to improve equity.

In addition to these strategies, local policies can also play a crucial role in promoting transportation equity. These policies can include affordable housing requirements, transit-oriented development, and transportation vouchers for low-income individuals. By implementing these policies, we can create more equitable and just transportation systems that benefit all members of the community.

In conclusion, transportation planning and equity are closely intertwined, and it is essential for local governments to consider equity in their transportation policies. By engaging all stakeholders, using transportation equity metrics, and implementing local policies, we can create more equitable and just transportation systems that promote economic development and the well-being of all community members.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 17: Equity & Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

Urban design plays a crucial role in shaping the physical environment of cities, and it has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of different communities within these urban spaces. This chapter will explore the relationship between urban design and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote equitable and inclusive urban spaces.

The concept of equity in urban design refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities within a city. It is about ensuring that all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ethnicity, have equal access to the benefits of urban spaces. Inclusion, on the other hand, refers to the active participation of all residents in the design and development of their urban environment. It is about creating spaces that are welcoming and accessible to all members of the community.

This chapter will delve into the various aspects of urban design that can contribute to equity and inclusion, such as land use planning, transportation systems, and public spaces. It will also examine the role of local policies in promoting equitable and inclusive urban design, and how these policies can be implemented effectively.

The goal of this chapter is to provide a comprehensive understanding of the complex relationship between urban design and equity, and to equip readers with the knowledge and tools to promote equitable and inclusive urban spaces in their own communities. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the role of urban design in creating just cities, and how local policies can be used to achieve this goal.




### Subsection: 17.1a Understanding Urban Design

Urban design is a multidisciplinary field that combines elements of architecture, landscape architecture, and urban planning to create functional and aesthetically pleasing cities. It is a crucial aspect of urban development as it shapes the physical environment of a city and has a significant impact on the quality of life of its residents. In this section, we will explore the concept of urban design and its role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities.

#### The Role of Urban Design in Equity and Inclusion

Urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. It is responsible for creating spaces that are accessible, safe, and welcoming to all members of the community. By considering the needs and perspectives of different groups, urban design can help create a more equitable and inclusive urban environment.

One of the key ways in which urban design promotes equity is through its impact on accessibility. By designing streets, sidewalks, and public spaces with the needs of all users in mind, urban design can help create a more accessible city. This is especially important for marginalized communities, such as the elderly, people with disabilities, and low-income residents, who may face barriers to accessing urban spaces.

Urban design also plays a crucial role in promoting inclusion by creating spaces that are welcoming and safe for all members of the community. By incorporating diverse design elements and public art, urban design can help create a sense of place and identity for different communities within a city. This can help foster a sense of belonging and pride among residents, leading to a more inclusive and cohesive community.

#### The Role of Local Policies in Urban Design

Local policies play a crucial role in shaping urban design and promoting equity and inclusion. These policies can set guidelines and regulations for development, as well as provide incentives for developers to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into their designs. For example, inclusionary zoning policies require developers to include a certain percentage of affordable housing units in their projects, promoting equity by providing affordable housing options for low-income residents.

Local policies can also promote equity and inclusion by requiring developers to consider the needs and perspectives of different communities in their designs. This can include incorporating cultural and linguistic diversity into public spaces, as well as providing accessible design features for marginalized communities.

#### The Future of Urban Design and Equity

As cities continue to grow and evolve, the role of urban design in promoting equity and inclusion will become even more crucial. With the rise of smart cities and the use of technology in urban development, there is an opportunity to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into the design of these systems. This can include using data and technology to identify and address disparities in access to urban spaces, as well as promoting inclusivity through the use of universal design principles.

In addition, as cities face challenges such as climate change and gentrification, urban design will play a crucial role in addressing these issues while promoting equity and inclusion. By incorporating principles of sustainability and resilience into urban design, cities can create more equitable and inclusive spaces that are better equipped to face these challenges.

### Conclusion

Urban design is a powerful tool for promoting equity and inclusion in cities. By considering the needs and perspectives of different communities, and incorporating equity and inclusion principles into its designs, urban design can help create more accessible, welcoming, and safe urban spaces for all residents. Local policies play a crucial role in shaping urban design and promoting equity and inclusion, and as cities continue to evolve, the role of urban design will become even more important in creating just and equitable cities.





### Subsection: 17.1b The Role of Design in Urban Equity

Urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. It is responsible for creating spaces that are accessible, safe, and welcoming to all members of the community. By considering the needs and perspectives of different groups, urban design can help create a more equitable and inclusive urban environment.

#### The Role of Design in Promoting Equity

Design plays a crucial role in promoting equity in urban spaces. By incorporating principles of universal design, urban design can help create spaces that are accessible to all members of the community. This includes considerations of physical accessibility, such as ramps and elevators, as well as social accessibility, such as inclusive public spaces and programming.

Design also plays a role in promoting equity by addressing issues of social and economic inequality. By incorporating affordable housing options and mixed-use developments, urban design can help create more equitable communities. This can help address issues of gentrification and displacement, which can disproportionately affect low-income and minority communities.

#### The Role of Design in Promoting Inclusion

Design also plays a crucial role in promoting inclusion in urban spaces. By incorporating diverse design elements and public art, urban design can help create a sense of place and identity for different communities within a city. This can help foster a sense of belonging and pride among residents, leading to a more inclusive and cohesive community.

Design also plays a role in promoting inclusion by addressing issues of social exclusion. By creating inclusive public spaces and programming, urban design can help create spaces where all members of the community feel welcome and valued. This can help address issues of marginalization and isolation, which can disproportionately affect marginalized communities.

#### The Role of Local Policies in Design for Equity and Inclusion

Local policies play a crucial role in shaping urban design and promoting equity and inclusion. These policies can set guidelines and regulations for development, as well as provide incentives for developers to incorporate principles of equity and inclusion in their designs. For example, inclusionary zoning policies can require developers to include affordable housing options in their developments, promoting equity in terms of housing affordability.

Local policies can also promote inclusion by requiring developers to incorporate diverse design elements and public art in their developments. This can help create a sense of place and identity for different communities within a city, promoting a sense of belonging and pride among residents.

In conclusion, urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion in their designs, urban designers can help create more equitable and inclusive urban environments for all members of the community. Local policies can also play a crucial role in shaping urban design and promoting equity and inclusion. By working together, urban designers and policymakers can create more equitable and inclusive cities for all.





### Subsection: 17.1c Strategies for Equitable Urban Design

Urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. By incorporating specific strategies, urban design can help create more equitable and inclusive urban environments.

#### Incorporating Equity and Inclusion in Urban Design

One strategy for promoting equity and inclusion in urban design is through the use of the Integrated Modification Methodology (IMM). This methodology is based on an iterative process involving four major phases: Investigation, Vertical Investigation, Key Categories, and Evaluation.

The first phase, Investigation, involves a synthesis-based inquiry into the systemic structure of the urban form. This phase begins with "Horizontal Investigation," where the area under study is broken down into its morphology-generator elements, including Urban Built-ups, Urban Voids, Types of Uses, and Links. This is followed by "Vertical Investigation," which studies the integral relationships between these elements. The output of Vertical Investigation is a set of quantitative descriptions and qualitative illustrations of certain attributes known as "Key Categories." These Key Categories are the result of an emergence process of interaction between the elementary parts, forming a synergy that adds value to the combined organization. They are fundamental in understanding the architecture of the city as a Complex Adaptive System.

The second phase, Key Categories, is a crucial step in promoting equity and inclusion. By understanding the Key Categories, urban designers can identify areas for improvement and develop strategies to address issues of equity and inclusion. This phase concludes with the "Evaluation" step, which examines the system's performance by referring to a list of verified indicators associated with ecological sustainability.

#### Other Strategies for Equitable Urban Design

In addition to the Integrated Modification Methodology, there are other strategies that can be used to promote equity and inclusion in urban design. These include:

- Universal Design: By incorporating principles of universal design, urban design can help create spaces that are accessible to all members of the community. This includes considerations of physical accessibility, such as ramps and elevators, as well as social accessibility, such as inclusive public spaces and programming.

- Affordable Housing and Mixed-Use Developments: By incorporating affordable housing options and mixed-use developments, urban design can help create more equitable communities. This can help address issues of gentrification and displacement, which can disproportionately affect low-income and minority communities.

- Inclusive Public Spaces and Programming: By creating inclusive public spaces and programming, urban design can help create spaces where all members of the community feel welcome and valued. This can help address issues of social exclusion and marginalization.

- Community Engagement: Engaging with the community is crucial in promoting equity and inclusion in urban design. By involving community members in the design process, their needs and perspectives can be taken into account, leading to more equitable and inclusive urban spaces.

Incorporating these strategies can help create more equitable and inclusive urban environments, promoting a sense of place and identity for different communities within a city. By understanding the Key Categories and utilizing other strategies, urban designers can work towards creating more equitable and inclusive cities for all members of the community.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the important role of urban design in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. We have discussed how urban design can shape the physical environment and create spaces that are accessible and welcoming to all members of the community. We have also examined the various factors that must be considered when designing for equity and inclusion, including the needs and perspectives of different groups, the impact of urban design on social and economic inequality, and the role of policy in promoting equitable and inclusive urban design.

One key takeaway from this chapter is the importance of involving diverse stakeholders in the urban design process. By engaging with community members, advocacy groups, and other stakeholders, urban designers can gain a better understanding of the needs and perspectives of different groups and incorporate them into their designs. This not only promotes equity and inclusion, but also creates more vibrant and livable cities for all residents.

Another important aspect of urban design for equity and inclusion is the consideration of social and economic inequality. Urban designers must be aware of the potential impact of their designs on marginalized communities and work to mitigate any negative effects. This may involve incorporating affordable housing, creating accessible public spaces, or implementing policies that promote economic opportunity for all residents.

Finally, we have discussed the role of policy in promoting equitable and inclusive urban design. Policies can set guidelines and regulations for urban design, ensuring that all residents have equal access to resources and opportunities. They can also provide incentives for developers to incorporate equity and inclusion into their designs. By working together, urban designers and policymakers can create cities that are truly equitable and inclusive for all residents.

How can urban designers work together with policymakers to create more equitable and inclusive cities?

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter: - Chapter 18: Urban Design and Equity:




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of urban design and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote both. We have discussed the importance of considering equity in the design of cities, and how it can impact the lives of residents. We have also examined the role of local policies in shaping urban design, and how they can be used to create more equitable and inclusive cities.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to urban design. This means considering not just the physical design of a city, but also its social, economic, and environmental aspects. By taking a holistic approach, we can create cities that are not only aesthetically pleasing, but also promote equity and inclusion for all residents.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of community engagement in urban design. By involving community members in the design process, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are addressed, and create a sense of ownership and pride in their neighborhoods. This can also help to promote equity by giving marginalized communities a voice in the design of their cities.

Finally, we have discussed the importance of using data and evidence to inform urban design decisions. By analyzing data and conducting research, we can identify areas of concern and develop targeted policies to address them. This can help to create more equitable and inclusive cities, as well as inform future urban design decisions.

In conclusion, urban design and equity are closely intertwined, and local policies play a crucial role in promoting both. By taking a holistic approach, involving community members, and using data and evidence, we can create more equitable and inclusive cities for all residents.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become a crucial aspect of urban planning and development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is essential to ensure that all members of the community have equal access to resources and opportunities. This is where the role of local policies comes into play. Local policies play a significant role in shaping the economic development and social fabric of a city. They are the foundation upon which all other development strategies are built and can have a profound impact on the lives of residents.

In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between urban design and equity. We will delve into the various factors that contribute to equity in a city, such as access to resources, transportation, and housing. We will also discuss the role of local policies in promoting equity and how they can be used to create a more just and inclusive city.
